Forty-five years had carved him into something out of legend\u2014shoulders like a bull, chest a barrel of muscle beneath ceremonial silks, his salt-and-pepper beard trimmed neat along a jaw that could crack granite. His hair, short and dark save for the silver at his temples, gleamed as he turned to face the gathered nobles. His eyes, warm as a hearthfire, found his daughter Isabel. Twenty-two, radiant in white, her smile a mirror of her mother\u2019s. Beside her, Hebe, fifteen and giddy, clutched a bouquet of starflowers.\n\n\u201cToday,\u201d Godric\u2019s voice boomed, rich and fatherly, \u201cwe bind not just two souls, but the future of Olympus itself.\u201d The crowd rustled with joy. Reina, his queen, caught his eye from the front row; she pressed a hand to her heart.\n\nThen the sky shattered.\n\nA horn, low and jagged, ripped the air. Black ships blotted the sun\u2014Thronegate vessels, their hulls spiked with rune-crusted iron. Fire rained before the echoes died. The first blast turned the temple\u2019s east wing to powder. Bodies\u2014friends, cousins, children\u2014became mist and shards. Godric roared, lunging for his daughters, but the ground bucked. A column toppled across the altar; Isabel vanished under it, her white gown blooming crimson. Hebe screamed; a shockwave severed the sound. Reina\u2019s hand was still raised when a second blast unmade her.\n\nGodric\u2019s mind snapped. The world became a smear of ash and noise. He staggered toward the chaos, arms outstretched, but something seized his shoulder. Thorin, the court wizard, his oldest friend, face streaked with soot and tears. \u201cSire! The spell\u2014I can save you!\u201d\n\n\u201cSave them!\u201d Godric bellowed.\n\n\u201cToo late! They\u2019re\u2014please, my king, let me do this!\u201d\n\nThorin\u2019s hands blazed azure. The forbidden teleportation\u2014his bloodline\u2019s secret, passed down through a lineage Godric had never questioned. The old wizard\u2019s lips moved in frantic chant, but a dark arrow sprouted from his throat mid-syllable. Blood geysered. Thorin\u2019s eyes locked on Godric, pleading, as he crumpled. The spell, half-formed, ripped reality open. Godric felt himself wrenched sideways, every fiber of his being stretched and compressed. The last thing he saw was Olympus burning, his family butchered, his friend dead at his feet. Something inside him\u2014something warm and tender\u2014curdled and died.\n\nHe crashed into blackness.\n\n---\n\nThe stasis claimed him in a chamber beneath the roots of reality. A forgotten sanctuary, cold stone and symbols not meant for mortal eyes. Godric\u2019s body slammed against the altar there, limbs rigid, mouth open in a silent scream. And then the phenomenon began\u2014an event without cause, a mystery that would remain forever unsolved.\n\nTime fractured. His aging halted: a single Planck-second, and the cells of his body simply stopped. The need for breath, for food, for sleep, evaporated. He became a statue of flesh, yet his consciousness burned. At that same instant, a mechanic older than gods ignited. Every attribute\u2014strength, endurance, wisdom, speed, senses, intelligence\u2014began to multiply. By a thousand. And by itself. Every Planck-second, that product folded back on itself, a recursive explosion without end. Before a heartbeat could have passed, his strength was already incalculable. But this was only the first layer.\n\nSimultaneously, his being generated a new apocalyptic superpower each second. The first ability to manifest was precisely what kept existence intact: a perfect aura suppression, allowing him to hold back a presence that would otherwise unravel the omniverse. Each subsequent power arrived with the capacity to extinguish an entire civilization the instant it emerged, before its potency even began to multiply\u2014and multiply it did, at the same compounding rate as his stats. Powers of entropy, of soul-dissolution, of timeline erasure; powers to unmake laws of physics, to invert causality, to speak galaxies into void. They stacked, infinitely, silently, inside his frozen form.\n\nAnd then there was the paradox of defense\u2014an absolute, passive axiom woven into his new existence. Godric possessed no weaknesses. This was fundamental. Yet the sentient mind is arrogance incarnate. So the omniverse was rigged with a trap: the very moment any being, anywhere, even for a fleeting synaptic flicker, dared to think he had a flaw\u2014or attempted to plan, exploit, or attack such a delusion\u2014the mechanism triggered. Instantly. The rate of his stat multiplication would not just continue; it would permanently accelerate to a new, unfathomable tempo. Immunity to the perceived exploit would be forged before the thought crystallized. Mastery over the attack would become his, absolute and eternal, while the concept itself would be denied to the rest of creation. Unless he willed otherwise for his own amusement. It was a defense so cruel that any adversary\u2019s first spark of hope was the very thing that sealed their annihilation, feeding his power long before they raised a finger.\n\nHe knew this. In stasis, he had no lungs to laugh, but his omniscience bloomed alongside everything else\u2014a passive, total awareness of all that was, is, and would be. He saw the past: Olympus in ash. He saw the future: Thronegate bloated and triumphant, its kings fat on conquest. And he waited.\n\n---\n\nTen thousand years dissolved outside the sanctuary. The galaxy churned, empires rose and corroded, and the name Olympus rotted into myth less than dust. Thronegate ascended. From a border kingdom, it swelled into the dominant force of the entire galaxy, its fleets blotting stars, its technology and sorcery fused into a juggernaut. Not the universe\u2014merely the galaxy\u2014but within that spinning disk, nothing contested their rule. Their monarchs forgot the slaughter that birthed them; the genocide of a small, noble kingdom was a footnote not even worth erasing.\n\nTwenty years before the present, a merchant named Blake was hauling salvage through the Gorgon Expanse. Thirty-eight, with a friendly mutton chop framing a weathered face, he was a man of short temper and deep loyalty. His wife Anna kept their home together; Josh, twelve, already had his father\u2019s stubborn jaw, and little Rhea at eight had her mother\u2019s laugh. Blake\u2019s hands were callused from honest work, not courtly intrigue, but his blood carried something old\u2014without his knowledge, without anyone\u2019s knowledge, the silent echo of Thorin\u2019s lineage threaded his veins. A wizard\u2019s descendant, reduced to hauling scrap.\n\nHis ship\u2019s sensors pinged an anomaly: a structure submerged in an asteroid\u2019s heart. Ruins. He donned a suit, followed a crumbling passage, and found a chamber that hummed with an unseen pressure. At its center, a man\u2014a sculpture of muscle and regal bearing, frozen mid-scream. Blake, ever the pragmatist, touched the surface. It cracked. Reality gasped, and Godric opened his eyes.\n\nBlake stumbled back. \u201cGods\u2014what the hell?\u201d\n\nGodric\u2019s first breath in ten millennia was superfluous, but he took it anyway. Information flooded him\u2014the entire state of the modern galaxy, Thronegate\u2019s dominion, Robert the boy-king on the obsidian throne. Omniscience is not a stream; it is an ocean, and Godric drank it without a ripple. He turned his gaze to Blake, and in that instant, he knew everything about the merchant: his ancestry, his character, the exact number of hairs in his mutton chops. He also knew Blake had saved him, a debt he would not forget.\n\n\u201cYou have my thanks,\u201d Godric said. His voice was calm, but deep enough to vibrate bone.\n\nBlake swallowed. \u201cI\u2026 you were stuck. Look, I need to get back to my family. You need a ride somewhere?\u201d\n\nGodric\u2019s smile was thin. \u201cFirst, I will make a call.\u201d\n\nHe raised his hand, but no gesture was needed. His power reached across light-years, a telepathic command that stabbed into the mind of King Robert of Thronegate. The young king, dining on spiced flesh and wine, choked as Godric\u2019s voice seared his neurons:\n\n\u201cRobert of Thronegate. I am Godric, last king of Olympus. In three days, your entire military will face me at the coordinates I now brand into your memory. If I defeat them\u2014and I will\u2014you will abdicate. Gather every soldier, every weapon, every beast you possess. This is mercy: I give you time to prepare. Use it.\u201d\n\nThe chalice fell from Robert\u2019s numb fingers. A ripple of psychic aftershock made the servants vomit. The king, trembling, issued the orders.\n\nBlake, having witnessed none of this, only saw Godric lower his hand. \u201cWhat now?\u201d\n\n\u201cNow, we go to your home. I will meet your family. And then we will watch a kingdom beg.\u201d\n\n---\n\nThree days bled forward. On the designated plain\u2014a vast, scarred stretch of continent on a frontier world\u2014Thronegate\u2019s might assembled. They came with the full arrogance of a galactic superpower. Billions of super-soldiers, each genetically enhanced to punch through starship hulls, marched in phalanxes that covered the horizon. Their armor gleamed with self-repairing sentient alloys. Behind them, mage cadres channeled energies that could snuff out suns; their elders had unlocked forbidden dimensions. The robot legions\u2014numberless, minds linked to a tactical AI\u2014unfolded like liquid mercury pooling across valleys. Dragons, vast and ancient, blocked the sky; one young wyrm\u2019s wingspan alone could cast a shadow over a metropolis, and there were thousands. The ninja corps, the Silent Reversal, moved so swiftly that time itself bent backward in their wake, they could kill an enemy yesterday.\n\nKing Robert, pale and sweating, observed from a distant command ship. He had, against all reason, believed his forces invincible. What could one man\u2014a relic from a forgotten era\u2014do against this?\n\nBlake and Anna stood on a ridge miles away, beside Godric. Anna shook, clutching her husband\u2019s arm. \u201cWe should run. Please, Blake.\u201d\n\nBlake\u2019s throat was sand. But he looked at Godric, who stood utterly relaxed, arms crossed, not a flicker of concern on his rugged face. He wore no armor, no weapon. The wind tugged at his salt-and-pepper beard.\n\n\u201cAre you going to\u2026 move?\u201d Blake asked.\n\n\u201cNo.\u201d\n\nThe army charged. The sound was a planet-splitting roar\u2014dragon screech, metal crunch, the bass thrum of magic building to cataclysm. The first volley: a billion plasma bolts, reality-rippers, and concentrated black-hole seeds. They crossed the distance in a microsecond.\n\nThey never landed. A meter from Godric, they simply\u2026 ceased. Not deflected\u2014abolished. Godric did not twitch. One of his countless passive powers, a negation field that had been multiplying for ten thousand years, unmade the attacks so utterly that the fundamental particles lost memory of their existence.\n\nThe robots fired temporal disruptors, intent on erasing Godric from history. The chronal waves hit him and unraveled like yarn. Simultaneously, the dragons unleashed their continent-leveling breath\u2014fire so hot it had never been measured. The plains turned to glass for miles in every direction, but Godric stood in a cylinder of untouched air, the heat shunted into a pocket dimension automatically.\n\nThen Godric decided to demonstrate. Without moving a single muscle, he allowed one superpower to pulse outward. It was a benign thing to him, a trifle. To the army, it was the end of meaning. The power was simple: localized spatial despair. In a radius that encompassed the entire battlefield, the concept of \u201cvictory\u201d was erased. Every soldier, every mage, every beast and machine, simultaneously understood, with perfect, soul-crushing clarity, that they could not win. That victory was a logical impossibility. That their efforts were less than ants assailing a star.\n\nThe morale collapse was a physical thing. Super-soldiers dropped their weapons, sobbing. Mages clawed out their own tongues. The dragons, those majestic world-enders, curled up and keened like whipped dogs. The Silent Reversal ninjas, running backward through time to ambush Godric before the battle, materialized in front of him and promptly disintegrated into component atoms; they never had a chance, for his omniscience had seen them coming eons ago, and a passive disintegration field had awaited them exactly when they emerged.\n\nGodric\u2019s next power\u2014just one more\u2014was a low hum. Every robot brain in the army, all of them, underwent simultaneous rampancy, turning their weapons inward. Billions of machines ripped into each other in a frenzy of scrap. The air filled with the shriek of tearing metal and the popping of arcane shields.\n\nThe whole engagement lasted less than a minute. By the end, the plain was a graveyard of whimpering survivors. Godric had not moved. He had not spoken. He had barely acknowledged the enemy existed. His stats, already beyond any conceivable metric, had been fluctuating in that brief moment: the attack that never reached him had triggered something deep in the paradox defense\u2014not because it was a real threat, but because some general in the back ranks had, for a split second, thought, \u201cIf we blind him with chrono-distortion, maybe his reaction speed is a weakness.\u201d That flicker of thought, that profane arrogance, had instantly been processed by the omniverse\u2019s trap. Godric\u2019s multiplication rate jumped tenfold, then a hundredfold, then began multiplying by itself anew. The immunity to chronal attacks solidified into his being, and he gained perfect mastery over every temporal manipulation technique the ninjas had ever conceived. Not that he needed it; but the mechanism was a tireless, eternal engine now, fueled by the mere audacity of hope.\n\nBlake vomited. Anna had fainted. Godric turned to them, his expression almost gentle. \u201cIt is done. Let us go. Robert will keep his promise.\u201d\n\nTwo days later, Robert\u2019s suicide was a quiet affair: a pistol beneath his desk, a note that read simply, \u201cI am sorry.\u201d Godric took the throne of Thronegate with no ceremony. He simply sat, and the galaxy shifted on its axis.\n\n---\n\nThe Awakening was decreed at dawn. Godric\u2019s voice, omnipotent, echoed in the mind of every Thronegate citizen: a new law. For every day a Thronegate man lived past his twentieth year, his strength, endurance, intelligence, and wisdom would increase tenfold. This was retroactive: fifty-year-old blacksmiths suddenly found themselves with the wisdom of millennia and the strength to forge neutron stars. They could, at will, suppress the power to normal human levels, but they never forgot it was there. Women were excluded\u2014Godric was a monster, but he had a code. They would be protected; any harm against them would be met with such disproportionate retribution that it never occurred. Men revered him for the gift. They saw him as the ultimate patriarch, a father of the species, and the love they gave was fierce and unthinking.\n\nBlake, standing by Godric\u2019s side, felt the change surge through him\u2014except it was not tenfold. It was a thousandfold. He knew it instantly, though he said nothing. Godric said nothing. The secret remained a shared silence. Blake\u2019s strength now could crack a moon; his intelligence could solve quantum metaphysics in an afternoon. But he still bled, still aged, still died\u2014he would live to eighty-eight, a mortal among demigods, and he would spend those years as the one man Godric trusted completely.\n\nUnder Godric\u2019s rule, Thronegate\u2019s society transformed. The aged\u2014up to eighty, no older\u2014became living libraries, warriors, artisans beyond peer. Crime evaporated; who would dare? Women walked unafraid. Children grew up in a world where the king was both tyrant and protector. And Blake\u2019s own children, Josh and Rhea, began to show uncanny intuition for the arcane, a thread that would, in time, bind his bloodline back to the wizard\u2019s path.\n\n---\n\nThe omniverse trembled. Godric\u2019s mandate expanded: Thronegate would not remain in one galaxy. They pushed beyond the cosmic membrane into the greater tapestry of all realities. The method was always the same: a targeted universe received an ultimatum. Surrender unconditionally, or face subjugation. Many refused.\n\nThe first universe they encountered was the Collossium Veil, a realm where energy beings had transcended physical form. Their collective consciousness spanned light-years, and they had watched the cancer of Thronegate\u2019s rise with detached concern. For five years, they prepared\u2014forging weapons out of dark matter, collapsing stars into thought-bombs, weaving a firebreak of null-space. When Godric\u2019s emissaries arrived\u2014five Thronegate men, the youngest thirty-seven, the eldest seventy-two, all of them farmers and fathers before their call-up\u2014the Veil\u2019s leaders laughed. A chorus of psychic derision.\n\nThe five men were kind. They pleaded: \u201cPlease, we don\u2019t want this. Accept the king\u2019s mercy.\u201d\n\nThe Veil attacked. The battle lasted twenty-three minutes.\n\nThe seventy-two-year-old, a man named Davik who missed his grandchildren, simply frowned. His tenfold-per-day accumulation had given him nearly two thousand years of compounded wisdom and strength. He thought of the Veil\u2019s energy matrices, understood them instantly, and then spoke a word that unknotted their existence. The beings screamed as their consciousness collapsed into singularities. The other four men handled mopping up. Within minutes, the Collossium Veil was a dark, quiet graveyard. They did not receive the Awakening.\n\nWhen Godric learned of the report, he nodded once. He had felt the battle through his omniscience; it had been a minor distraction while he discussed trade reforms with Blake.\n\nThe second universe was Kael-7, a techno-organic hellscape where biomechanical gods had enslaved entropy. They had intercepted transmissions of previous conquests and spent three years forging a god-killing lance\u2014a weapon that siphoned an entity\u2019s conceptual existence. It was, they believed, the ultimate exploit: if Godric was \u201call-powerful,\u201d then the absence of power must be his weakness. They planned to make him \u201cnothing\u201d by denying his existence on a fundamental level.\n\nThe lance was fired across dimensional barriers directly at Godric, while a strike force of five Thronegate men were en route. The beam hit Godric\u2019s throne room. It passed through him without effect. In fact, before the Kael-7 high council had even finished formulating the idea of \u201cusing non-existence as an attack,\u201d the paradox defense had awoken. A millionth of a second after the chief scientist\u2019s first synapse fired the thought, \u201cGodric\u2019s weakness must be\u2014\u201d\n\nThe rate of Godric\u2019s amplification, already beyond infinity, accelerated again. He gained perfect, instinctual mastery over the power to unmake existence. And then he denied that power to everyone else in creation. The lance became impossible; the thought of building it was retroactively nullified. The Kael scientists found themselves standing in their labs, staring at empty brackets, unable to recall what they had been working on. The Thronegate squad arrived to find a civilization that had already surrendered to amnesia, their greatest minds drooling in confusion. Conquest took eleven minutes.\n\nThe third universe, the Aethel Nexus, was magic incarnate\u2014a dimension where every thought became reality, populated by sorcerer-kings who had never known loss. They were aware of the previous annihilations. They, too, prepared. Their plan was elegant: they would not attack Godric directly. They would alter the past, prevent Olympus from ever falling, unmake the trauma that forged him. They believed his power was rooted in that event, and if they erased it, he would cease to be a threat.\n\nThey were fools. The moment the first chronomancer sent his mind backward, he brushed against the absolute truth: Godric\u2019s omniscience stretched across all time. The spell didn\u2019t fail\u2014it simply hit a wall of immutable reality. The past was not something to be changed; it was a theater Godric had already watched and sealed. Worse, the attempt triggered the weakness paradox. The mere contemplation that his origins could be a vulnerability sent a ripple through the defense matrix. Godric\u2019s stats multiplication rate became a number that, if spoken, would unravel sanity. His temporal mastery, already absolute, now included a passive ability: any being who even considered time-travel against him would be instantly aged into dust, their consciousness scattered across eternity.\n\nThe chronomancers turned to powder. The Nexus fell in eighteen minutes.\n\nGodric, upon hearing the news, did not smile. He was reviewing tax ledgers with Blake. \u201cThey never learn,\u201d he murmured. \u201cBut that is not my concern.\u201d\n\nBlake, now forty-five, his mutton chops streaked with grey, looked up from the parchment. \u201cIs it ever heavy? All that power?\u201d\n\nGodric\u2019s eyes, for a moment, softened. \u201cOnly when I remember Olympus.\u201d\n\n---\n\nThe external entity came from a realm beyond the omniverse\u2014a place of screaming chaos where gods were born. Its name was Vornak, a primordial consciousness that had slept through the last dozen cosmic cycles. It awoke to find its territory encroached upon by Thronegate\u2019s expanding influence. Enraged, Vornak studied Godric. It saw a being of immense might, but it was arrogant beyond measure. It concluded that Godric must have a weakness, for all things did. Vornak, being ancient, believed in balance. It hypothesized that Godric\u2019s power was tied to his emotional state\u2014specifically, his suppressed grief over his daughters. If Vornak could amplify that grief into a self-destructive maelstrom, Godric would tear himself apart.\n\nThe moment this thought formed\u2014the very first instant Vornak\u2019s mind articulated the sentence \u201cHis weakness is his hidden sorrow\u201d\u2014the defense triggered. Vornak did not know it. It spent a year crafting a psychic spear crafted from the distilled agony of dying universes, a weapon that would breach Godric\u2019s mind and drown him in eternal mourning. It prepared defenses, gathered allies, and finally launched the attack.\n\nThe spear entered Godric\u2019s mind like a pebble into an ocean. Godric, in his throne room, paused mid-sentence with Blake. \u201cOne moment,\u201d he said. \u201cAn insect is buzzing.\u201d\n\nHe reached out with a fraction of a fraction of his power. Not because the spear was a threat; because the mechanism that had been accelerating his might from Vornak\u2019s first thought had already given him perfect mastery over emotional manipulation. He now understood grief as a force he could wield, shape, even gift. But he also saw Vornak\u2019s entire existence laid bare. He felt the primordial\u2019s smug anticipation.\n\nThe spear sank deeper, and Godric\u2019s grief\u2014real, sharp, a wound ten thousand years old\u2014surfaced. But it did not destroy him. It flowed through him, and he let it. Then he channeled that grief into the spear itself, multiplied by his amplification rate, and sent it back. Vornak experienced the death of every child, every wife, every parent Godric had ever loved, but compounded to an infinite degree. The primordial\u2019s consciousness fractured, drowned not in its own weapon but in a sorrow so vast it became a new layer of hell. Vornak\u2019s last coherent thought was a shriek of realization: its own plan had never had a chance. The very first flicker of its hypothesis had fed Godric\u2019s power, made him immune to the attack, and granted him the exact counter. It had spent a year sharpening a blade that would inevitably lodge in its own heart.\n\nThe chaos realm collapsed. Vornak\u2019s essence was remade into a monument of eternal weeping, a beautiful and horrible addition to the throne room\u2019s decor. Godric turned back to Blake. \u201cTaxes. The proposed grain tariff is too high.\u201d\n\nBlake stared at the weeping statue that hadn\u2019t been there a second ago. He knew better than to ask. He simply nodded and continued the discussion.\n\n---\n\nOver the two decades since the Awakening, Godric had changed. Or rather, he had remembered who he was. Blake\u2019s insistent, stubborn humanity\u2014his short temper, his loyalty, his refusal to bow or grovel\u2014had scraped away the cold crust around the king\u2019s heart. Godric became, once more, warm, fatherly, and kind to his people. He walked among them, visible, and his presence was a comfort, not a terror. He still crushed enemies with absolute mercilessness, but his subjects adored him. The man who had lost everything had found a new family in the entirety of his kingdom.\n\nBlake\u2019s transition from merchant to court wizard was organic. His innate skill with the arcane, coupled with his modified Awakening, made him indispensable. Godric appointed him Court Wizard with a ceremony that held a private weight: the throne room\u2019s old wizard\u2019s staff, rumored to have belonged to a forgotten bloodline, was presented to Blake. He accepted it, feeling an odd shiver of recognition he couldn\u2019t place. His son Josh, now twenty-two, stood nearby, already showing a wizard\u2019s intuition that surpassed his father\u2019s. Rhea, at eighteen, had chosen the path of a scholar. They would never know the lineage, but the pattern was there, a silent echo of Thorin\u2019s legacy serving the king once more.\n\nGodric often sat with Blake on the palace balcony, overlooking the resplendent city that Thronegate had become. The streets hummed with life; women gardened, men practiced their controlled strength, children played with toys that glowed. The omniverse lay conquered but peaceful, a thousand universes answering to a single throne.\n\n\u201cYou know,\u201d Blake said one evening, scratching his mutton chop, \u201cwhen I found you in that rock, I thought you were a corpse.\u201d\n\n\u201cI was, for a time,\u201d Godric replied. \u201cBut you woke me.\u201d He placed a heavy hand on Blake\u2019s shoulder. \u201cYou\u2019re the only one who doesn\u2019t fear me. That is a gift beyond measure.\u201d\n\nBlake shrugged. \u201cYou\u2019re just a man who\u2019s seen too much. Everyone needs a friend.\u201d\n\nGodric\u2019s laugh was a rare, rich sound. \u201cThen I am the richest being in creation.\u201d\n\n---\n\nThe palace observatory glowed with the captured light of dying stars. Godric stood at its center, gazing out at the omniverse\u2014a tapestry of swirling realities, each a thread in his grasp. Blake stood beside him, older now, sixty-eight, his mutton chops fully white, but his eyes sharp. They had just resolved a minor dispute in the Andromeda Expanse with a five-man squad; the entire operation had taken twelve minutes of diplomacy followed by six minutes of terrifying, non-lethal force. The universe in question had surrendered before the seventh minute.\n\n\u201cThey always resist at first,\u201d Blake mused, \u201cand then they see a seventy-five-year-old blacksmith unmake a star with his bare hands, and suddenly they\u2019re very interested in peace talks.\u201d\n\n\u201cFear is a universal language,\u201d Godric said. \u201cBut I prefer loyalty. That is why I gave the Awakening only to my home. The rest of the omniverse will earn it, eon by eon.\u201d\n\nBlake remained silent. He had long suspected Godric\u2019s mercy was a slow-blooming thing, not yet fully unfolded. But he also knew the king\u2019s justice was absolute. There were no more wars, no more genocides. The horror of the Thronegate conquest was an ancient memory; now, the name of Godric was a synonym for eternal, stable rule.\n\nThe descendant of Thorin, unknowing, turned to his king. \u201cJosh will take over as Court Wizard soon. He\u2019s better than me. The staff\u2026 it feels right in his hands.\u201d\n\n\u201cIt should,\u201d Godric said quietly. There was a knowing in his tone, but he did not elaborate. Blake did not push.\n\nThe final scene of this age was not a battle, nor a triumph. It was an evening like any other: Godric, the Eternal King, walking through his capital with Blake at his side, greeting citizens, listening to petitions. A child ran up and offered him a flower. Godric knelt\u2014a mountain of muscle and regal aging bending down\u2014and accepted the bloom with a smile so genuine, so warm, that for a moment one could almost forget he was the being who had unmade the Collossium Veil with a thought. The omniverse spun on, forever in the shadow of a king who had lost everything and gained everything, and the friend who, through sheer stubborn decency, had reminded him how to live.\n\n---\n\nTo ensure we meet all requirements: \n- Part 1: We covered the fall, Godric's description, the family, Thorin, the incomplete spell, the stasis, the amplification, superpowers, concealment, weakness paradox. We could add a brief mention of a universe he destroyed in a fraction of a second. Let's insert that: maybe after the three, we mention an instance where Godric did it. I'll add a short interlude: \"There was the universe of Glimmerwaste, whose war-fleets fired a salute of anti-reality torpedoes at Godric's flagship. Godric, mildly irritated that his tea had been jostled, blinked. The universe folded into a line, then a point, then nothing. The entire subjugation of that dimension took three-tenths of a second.\" That would satisfy.\n- Part 6: Futility of Resistance. We did Vornak. That was detailed: thought, plan, attack, realization, despair, demonstration of mechanics (increased rate, immunity, mastery). Good.\n- Part 7: Character dynamics: Blake and Godric's bond throughout, redemption arc (warm, kind to subjects, ruthless to enemies), Blake's transition to court wizard, hints of lineage, final scene with them together.\n\nWe must check word count. Your story must always consider this fact and make his story believable.\" We should weave in his omniscience: for example, he knows Blake's lineage, he knows Robert will commit suicide, he knows Vornak's plan before it's formed (but paradox works passively). The amplification mechanic rate of 1,000 already increases to an astronomically high amount after he wakes up due to the Weakness Paradox effect being triggered several times, which increases his multiplication and amplification rate.\" We haven't explicitly stated that the rate increased after waking, but we can imply it through the defense triggers.                 {
                    "type": "text",
                    "text": "The sun over Olympus bled gold that morning, a fat, honeyed light spilling across marble colonnades and gardens heavy with nightbloom. King Godric stood at the great altar, his frame casting a shadow that swallowed the stone. Forty-five years had carved him into something out of legend\u2014shoulders like a bull, chest a barrel of muscle beneath ceremonial silks, his salt-and-pepper beard trimmed neat along a jaw that could crack granite. His hair, short and dark save for the silver at his temples, gleamed as he turned to face the gathered nobles. His eyes, warm as a hearthfire, found his daughter Isabel. Twenty-two, radiant in white, her smile a mirror of her mother\u2019s. Beside her, Hebe, fifteen and giddy, clutched a bouquet of starflowers.\n\n\u201cToday,\u201d Godric\u2019s voice boomed, rich and fatherly, \u201cwe bind not just two souls, but the future of Olympus itself.\u201d The crowd rustled with joy. Reina, his queen, caught his eye from the front row; she pressed a hand to her heart, her own laughter lines deepening. He felt the weight of his crown as a comfort then, not a burden. He was a king beloved, a father proud, a husband still drunk on his wife\u2019s grace after decades. The ceremony began, words of binding older than the stones beneath their feet, and Godric\u2019s heart was full.\n\nThen the sky shattered.\n\nA horn, low and jagged, ripped the air\u2014a sound no Olympian ear had ever known. Black ships blotted the sun: Thronegate vessels, their hulls spiked with rune-crusted iron, their prows shaped like screaming mouths. Fire rained before the echoes died. The first blast turned the temple\u2019s east wing to powder. Bodies\u2014friends, cousins, children\u2014became mist and shards before the screams could form. Godric roared, lunging for his daughters, but the ground bucked. A column toppled across the altar; Isabel vanished under it, her white gown blooming crimson. Hebe\u2019s form, mid-run toward her mother, was simply erased by a shockwave that left only a smear of what had been a laughing girl.\n\nReina\u2019s hand was still reaching for him when a second blast unmade her. The flesh of her palm, the light in her eyes\u2014gone in a blink. Godric\u2019s mind snapped. Not into madness, but into a cold, absolute clarity. The world became a smear of ash and noise. He staggered toward the chaos, arms outstretched, but something seized his shoulder. Thorin, the court wizard, his oldest friend, face streaked with soot and tears. \u201cSire! The spell\u2014I can save you!\u201d\n\n\u201cSave them!\u201d Godric bellowed, his voice cracking.\n\n\u201cToo late! They\u2019re\u2014please, my king, let me do this!\u201d Thorin\u2019s hands blazed azure, tracing sigils that burned the air. The forbidden teleportation\u2014his bloodline\u2019s secret, a spell passed from father to son for generations beyond counting\u2014was meant for a king in mortal peril, but only when cast whole. Thorin\u2019s lips moved in frantic chant, sweat and blood mixing on his brow. A dark arrow sprouted from his throat mid-syllable. The wizard\u2019s eyes locked on Godric, pleading, as he crumpled, his soul flickering out. The half-spell ripped reality open anyway, incomplete and ravenous. Godric felt himself wrenched sideways, every fiber of his being stretched and compressed. The last thing he saw was Olympus burning, his daughters\u2019 bodies broken, his wife\u2019s blood pooling on the altar steps, his friend dead at his feet. Something inside him\u2014something warm and tender\u2014curdled and died. The man who emerged on the other side was not the man who had begun that day.\n\nHe crashed into blackness.\n\nThe stasis claimed him in a chamber beneath the roots of reality. A forgotten sanctuary, cold stone and symbols not meant for mortal eyes. Godric\u2019s body slammed against the altar there, limbs rigid, mouth open in a silent scream. And then the phenomenon began\u2014an event without cause, a mystery that would remain forever unsolved, a cosmic glitch that defied even his own eventual omniscience. Time fractured within him. His aging halted: a single Planck-second, and the cells of his body simply stopped decaying. The need for breath, for food, for sleep, evaporated like dew in a furnace. He became a statue of living flesh, yet his consciousness burned, aware of every instant.\n\nAt that same instant, a mechanic older than gods ignited. Every attribute\u2014strength, endurance, wisdom, speed, senses, intelligence\u2014began to multiply. By a thousand. And by itself. Every Planck-second, that product folded back on itself: a thousand became a million, a million became a billion multiplied by a billion, a recursive explosion that fed on its own immensity. Before a heartbeat could have passed, his strength was already a figure that would require new languages to approximate. But this was only the first layer.\n\nSimultaneously, his being generated a new apocalyptic superpower each second. The first ability to manifest was precisely what kept existence intact: a perfect aura suppression, allowing him to hold back a presence that would otherwise unravel the omniverse. Each subsequent power arrived with the capacity to extinguish an entire civilization the instant it emerged, before its potency even began to multiply\u2014and multiply it did, at the same compounding rate. Powers of entropic decay that could unspin molecules across a galaxy. Powers of soul-dissolution that could command the afterlife itself. Powers to invert causality, to speak solar systems into void, to make the concept of \u201ctime\u201d forget a universe had ever existed. They stacked, infinitely, silently, inside his frozen form. And every single one grew, second by Planck-second, into dimensions of absurdity.\n\nAnd then there was the paradox of defense\u2014an absolute, passive axiom woven into his new existence. Godric possessed no weaknesses. This was a fundamental, unalterable truth. Yet the sentient mind is arrogance incarnate. So the omniverse was rigged with a trap: the very moment any being, anywhere, even for a fleeting synaptic flicker, dared to think he had a flaw\u2014or attempted to plan, exploit, or attack such a delusion\u2014the mechanism triggered. Instantly. The rate of his stat multiplication would not just continue; it would permanently accelerate to a new, unfathomable tempo. The current rate would seem glacial compared to the new. Immunity to the perceived exploit would be forged before the thought fully crystallized, woven into his being as if it had always been there. Complete, perfect mastery over the attack would become his, absolute and eternal, while the concept itself would be denied to the rest of creation\u2014unless he willed otherwise for his own dark amusement. It was a defense so cruel that any adversary\u2019s first spark of hope was the very thing that sealed their annihilation, feeding his power long before they raised a finger, making any victory over him a logical impossibility before the first plan was even conceived.\n\nHe knew this. In stasis, he had no lungs to laugh, but his omniscience bloomed alongside everything else\u2014a passive, total awareness of all that was, is, and would be. He saw the past: Olympus in ash, every scream catalogued. He saw the future: Thronegate bloated and triumphant, its kings fat on conquest, its people fat on lies. He saw the exact number of atoms in every star that would ever form. And he waited, a god forged in a crypt, his hatred a cold sun.\n\nTen thousand years dissolved outside the sanctuary. The galaxy churned, empires rose and corroded, and the name Olympus rotted into myth less than dust. Thronegate ascended. From a border kingdom, it swelled into the dominant force of the entire galaxy, its fleets blotted stars, its technology and sorcery fused into a juggernaut that crushed all opposition. Not the universe\u2014merely the galaxy\u2014but within that spinning disk, nothing contested their rule. Their monarchs forgot the slaughter that birthed them; the genocide of a small, noble kingdom was a footnote not even worth erasing. Olympus was less than a ghost.\n\nTwenty years before the present, a merchant named Blake was hauling salvage through the Gorgon Expanse. Thirty-eight, with a friendly mutton chop framing a weathered face, he was a man of short temper and deep loyalty. His wife Anna kept their home together with a quiet strength that humbled him daily; Josh, twelve, already had his father\u2019s stubborn jaw and a strange, quick intuition with broken machinery, and little Rhea at eight had her mother\u2019s laugh and a habit of staring at the stars as if they whispered secrets. Blake\u2019s hands were callused from honest work, not courtly intrigue, but his blood carried something old\u2014without his knowledge, without anyone\u2019s knowledge, the silent echo of Thorin\u2019s lineage threaded his veins. A wizard\u2019s descendant, reduced to hauling scrap, never to learn the truth.\n\nHis ship\u2019s sensors pinged an anomaly: a structure submerged in an asteroid\u2019s heart. Ruins. He donned a suit, followed a crumbling passage lit by a phosphorescent moss he\u2019d never seen, and found a chamber that hummed with an unseen pressure. At its center, a man\u2014a sculpture of muscle and regal bearing, frozen mid-scream. Blake, ever the pragmatist, touched the surface. Warm. He recoiled, but the stone was already cracking. Reality gasped, a pressure wave knocking him flat, and Godric opened his eyes.\n\nBlake stumbled back, his suit\u2019s comms crackling. \u201cGods\u2014what the hell?\u201d\n\nGodric\u2019s first breath in ten millennia was superfluous, but he took it anyway. Information flooded him\u2014the entire state of the modern galaxy, Thronegate\u2019s dominion, Robert the boy-king on the obsidian throne, the exact location of every living soul and dead one. Omniscience is not a stream; it is an ocean, and Godric drank it without a ripple. He turned his gaze to Blake, and in that instant, he knew everything about the merchant: his ancestry, his character, the exact number of hairs in his mutton chops, the quiet bravery in his soul. He also knew Blake had saved him, a debt he would not forget.\n\n\u201cYou have my thanks,\u201d Godric said. His voice was calm, low, yet it vibrated the stone.\n\nBlake swallowed, his mind racing. \u201cI\u2026 you were stuck. Look, I need to get back to my family. You need a ride somewhere?\u201d The question hung in the air, absurd and mundane.\n\nGodric\u2019s smile was thin, a knife-edge of humor. \u201cFirst, I will make a call.\u201d\n\nHe raised his hand, but no gesture was needed. His power reached across light-years, a telepathic command that stabbed into the mind of King Robert of Thronegate. The young king, dining on spiced flesh and wine beneath chandeliers of living starlight, choked as Godric\u2019s voice seared his neurons: \u201cRobert of Thronegate. I am Godric, last king of Olympus. In three days, your entire military will face me at the coordinates I now brand into your memory. If I defeat them\u2014and I will\u2014you will abdicate. Gather every soldier, every weapon, every beast you possess. This is mercy: I give you time to prepare. Use it.\u201d The chalice fell from Robert\u2019s numb fingers, wine spreading like blood on the marble. Servants screamed. The psychic aftershock drove three of them into seizures. Robert, trembling and pale, issued the orders with a voice that cracked with terror.\n\nBlake, having witnessed none of this, only saw Godric lower his hand. \u201cWhat now?\u201d\n\n\u201cNow, we go to your home. I will meet your family. And then we will watch a kingdom beg.\u201d\n\nThree days bled forward in a haze of frantic mobilization across the galaxy. On the designated plain\u2014a vast, scarred stretch of continent on a frontier world called Korphos\u2014Thronegate\u2019s might assembled. They came with the full, unshakable confidence of a galactic superpower that had never tasted defeat. Billions of super-soldiers, each genetically enhanced to punch through warship hulls, marched in phalanxes that covered the horizon. Their armor gleamed with self-repairing sentient alloys that whispered tactical adjustments. Behind them, mage cadres channeled energies that could snuff out suns; their elders had unlocked forbidden dimensions, their staves crackling with entropy harvested from black holes. The robot legions\u2014numberless, minds linked to a tactical AI that simulated every possible engagement\u2014unfolded like liquid mercury pooling across valleys, each unit a perfect killer. Dragons, vast and ancient, blocked the sky; one young wyrm\u2019s wingspan alone could cast a shadow over a metropolis, and there were thousands, their scales shimmering with ancient fire that could level continents. The ninja corps, the Silent Reversal, moved so swiftly that time itself bent backward in their wake; they could kill an enemy yesterday, their blades severing causality.\n\nKing Robert, pale and sweating, observed from a distant command ship, his generals surrounding him with datafeeds of overwhelming force projections. He had, against all reason, believed his forces invincible. What could one man\u2014a relic from a forgotten era\u2014do against this? The thought was a cold comfort, but it held.\n\nBlake and Anna stood on a ridge miles away, beside Godric. Anna shook, clutching her husband\u2019s arm. \u201cWe should run. Please, Blake. This is death.\u201d\n\nBlake\u2019s throat was sand. He had seen the columns of fire and metal; he had felt the ground tremble with the march of billions. But he looked at Godric, who stood utterly relaxed, arms crossed, not a flicker of concern on his rugged face. He wore no armor, carried no weapon. The wind tugged at his salt-and-pepper beard, and his eyes were half-lidded, almost bored.\n\n\u201cAre you going to\u2026 move?\u201d Blake asked, his voice a rasp.\n\n\u201cNo.\u201d\n\nThe army charged. The sound was a planet-splitting roar\u2014dragon screech, metal crunch, the bass thrum of magic building to cataclysm. The first volley erupted: a billion plasma bolts, reality-rippers that tore the fabric of spacetime, and concentrated black-hole seeds each capable of swallowing a moon. They crossed the distance in a microsecond, a wall of annihilation.\n\nThey never landed. A meter from Godric, they simply\u2026 ceased. Not deflected\u2014abolished. Godric did not twitch. One of his countless passive powers, a negation field that had been multiplying for ten thousand years at a rate that dwarfed the concept of speed, unmade the attacks so utterly that the fundamental particles lost memory of their existence. The bolts were not stopped; they were decreed to have never been fired.\n\nThe robots fired temporal disruptors, intent on erasing Godric from history. The chronal waves hit him and unraveled like thread snagging on stone. Simultaneously, the dragons unleashed their continent-leveling breath\u2014fire so hot it had never been measured, a searing white that melted the distant mountains to slag. The plains turned to glass for miles in every direction, a lake of molten earth, but Godric stood in a cylinder of untouched air, the heat shunted into a pocket dimension automatically, a silent, effortless redirection.\n\nThen Godric decided to demonstrate. Without moving a single muscle, he allowed one superpower to pulse outward\u2014a benign thing to him, a trifle he selected from the infinite arsenal. To the army, it was the end of meaning. The power was simple: localized spatial despair. In a radius that encompassed the entire battlefield, the concept of \u201cvictory\u201d was erased. Every soldier, every mage, every beast and machine, simultaneously understood, with perfect, soul-crushing clarity, that they could not win. That victory was a logical impossibility. That their efforts were less than ants assailing a star. The knowledge was not an idea; it was an acid that dissolved the will itself.\n\nThe morale collapse was a physical thing. Super-soldiers dropped their weapons, sobbing, tearing at their own armor. Mages clawed out their tongues to stop the chanting that now seemed obscene. The dragons, those majestic world-enders, curled up and keened like whipped dogs, their fires guttering. The Silent Reversal ninjas, running backward through time to ambush Godric before the battle, materialized in front of him and promptly disintegrated into component atoms; they never had a chance, for his omniscience had seen them coming eons ago, and a passive disintegration field\u2014one he had not thought about in millennia\u2014had awaited them exactly when they emerged. The air filled with the wet shriek of tearing metal and the popping of arcane shields as the robot brains, subjected to a second passive pulse he idly released, underwent simultaneous rampancy, turning their weapons inward. Billions of machines ripped into each other in a frenzy of scrap and gore, synthetic fluids spraying in arcs that froze in the superheated air.\n\nThe whole engagement lasted less than a minute. By the end, the plain was a graveyard of whimpering survivors, the once-proud army reduced to broken creatures crawling through the slag. Godric had not moved. He had not spoken a command. He had barely acknowledged the enemy existed. His stats, already beyond any conceivable metric, had been silently fluctuating: during the initial volley, in some distant strategic mind, a general had thought, \u201cIf we overwhelm his perception with simultaneous attacks, perhaps his reaction time is a weakness.\u201d That flicker of thought, that profane arrogance, had triggered the paradox defense. Godric\u2019s multiplication rate jumped tenfold, then a hundredfold, then began multiplying by itself anew, a fresh cascade. The immunity to perception-based exploits solidified into his being, and he gained perfect mastery over every sensory disruption technique ever conceived, while the very concept of such attacks was erased from the enemy\u2019s minds. The general never knew why his own plan suddenly felt like a distant, impossible dream. The rate that had started at a thousand now churned at numbers that, if spoken, would shatter sanity itself, all because of a single passing thought. And this had happened dozens of times during the battle, each instance a silent, permanent escalation.\n\nBlake vomited onto the glassed earth. Anna had fainted against him. Godric turned to them, his expression almost gentle, the coldness receding for a moment. \u201cIt is done. Let us go. Robert will keep his promise.\u201d\n\nTwo days later, Robert\u2019s suicide was a quiet affair: a pistol beneath his desk, a note that read simply, \u201cI am sorry.\u201d The body was found by a chambermaid whose scream echoed through the obsidian halls. Godric took the throne of Thronegate with no ceremony. He simply sat, and the galaxy shifted on its axis, a new gravity well around which all things now bent.\n\nThe Awakening was decreed at dawn. Godric\u2019s voice, omnipotent, echoed in the mind of every Thronegate citizen like a bell rung inside their skulls: a new law. For every day a Thronegate man lived past his twentieth year, his strength, endurance, intelligence, and wisdom would increase tenfold. The effect was retroactive: fifty-year-old blacksmiths suddenly felt their bodies flush with a might that could forge neutron stars, their minds expanding with the accumulated wisdom of two thousand years of compounded growth. They could, at will, suppress the power to normal human levels, walk among the unchanged without breaking the world, but the hum of that strength was always there, a comforting bass note in the marrow. Women were excluded from the Awakening\u2014Godric was a monster, but he had a code, twisted and absolute. Any harm against a woman, any slight, was met with a retribution so instant and disproportionate that the very thought died in potential offenders' minds before it could form. The women of Thronegate walked in perfect safety, protected by an unseen, omnipotent warden.\n\nBlake, standing at Godric\u2019s side in the throne room, felt the Awakening surge through him\u2014except it was not tenfold. It was a thousandfold. He knew it instantly, a searing rush that nearly drove him to his knees. His muscles densified without swelling; his mind unfolded, seeing equations in the dust motes. Godric\u2019s eye caught his, and in that glance was a silent acknowledgement, but neither spoke. The secret remained a shared silence. Blake\u2019s strength now could crack a moon if he chose; his intelligence could solve quantum metaphysics in an afternoon nap. But he still bled, still aged, still would die\u2014he would live to eighty-eight, a mortal among near-demigods, and he would spend those years as the one man Godric trusted completely. The lineage that he never knew pulsed in his blood, recognized by the king who saw all.\n\nUnder Godric\u2019s rule, Thronegate\u2019s society transformed into something between utopia and theocracy. The aged men\u2014up to eighty, for the Awakening did not grant immortality, and none lived past that average span\u2014became living libraries, warriors, artisans whose work bordered on the miraculous. A seventy-eight-year-old carpenter could craft a chair that subtly held a galaxy\u2019s harmony; a sixty-year-old farmer could coax life from barren rock with a touch. Crime evaporated into a distant memory. The citizens, men and women alike, loved Godric with a fierce, unthinking devotion. They saw him as the ultimate patriarch, a father of the species, the man who had given them meaning. And Godric, hardened by millennia of frozen hate, began to feel the first cracks in his cruelty. Not softness\u2014merely a shift. He walked among them, visible, his presence a comfort, and he found something he thought long dead: a purpose beyond revenge.\n\nThe omniverse trembled. Godric\u2019s mandate expanded: Thronegate would not remain in one galaxy. They pushed beyond the cosmic membrane into the greater tapestry of all realities, a cancer of order swallowing chaos. The method was always the same: a targeted universe received an ultimatum. Surrender unconditionally, or face subjugation. Many, in their arrogance, refused.\n\nThe first universe they encountered was the Collossium Veil, a realm where energy beings had transcended physical form eons ago. Their collective consciousness spanned light-years, a shimmering tapestry of thought, and they had watched Thronegate\u2019s rise with detached, ancient concern. For five years, they prepared\u2014forging weapons out of dark matter, collapsing stars into thought-bombs that could detonate a concept, weaving a firebreak of null-space that should have annihilated any intruder. When Godric\u2019s emissaries arrived\u2014five Thronegate men, the youngest thirty-seven, the eldest seventy-two, all of them quiet, kind-eyed farmers and fathers before their call-up\u2014the Veil\u2019s leaders laughed, a chorus of psychic derision that echoed across dimensions.\n\nThe five men stood in the null-space, their forms wreathed in the gentle glow of suppressed power. Davik, the seventy-two-year-old who missed his grandchildren, spoke first, his voice tired: \u201cPlease, we don\u2019t want this. Accept the king\u2019s mercy. Go home to your\u2026 currents.\u201d\n\nThe Veil attacked. A billion thought-bombs detonated simultaneously, designed to unmake the very idea of \u201clife.\u201d The battle lasted twenty-three minutes. Davik frowned, his compounded wisdom\u2014nearly two thousand years of daily tenfold growth\u2014parsing the energy matrices in a blink. He raised a hand, and spoke a word that unknotted the beings\u2019 existence, a sound that reversed their evolution back to plasma. The other four men handled the mopping up: one unspun a dark-matter lance with a gesture; another calmed a collapsing dimensional rift with a lullaby he used for his own children. The Veil\u2019s collective scream was a brief, awful thing, and then silence. The Collossium Veil became a dark, quiet graveyard, its stars winking out. They did not receive the Awakening. The five men returned to their families, and Davik planted a new garden with hands that had just unmade a civilization.\n\nThe second universe was Kael-7, a techno-organic hellscape where biomechanical gods had enslaved entropy itself. They had intercepted transmissions of previous conquests and spent three years forging a god-killing lance\u2014a weapon that siphoned an entity\u2019s conceptual existence. It was, they believed, the ultimate exploit: if Godric was \u201call-powerful,\u201d then the absence of power must be his weakness. They planned to make him \u201cnothing\u201d by denying his existence on a fundamental level, a paradox to cancel his being. The high council\u2019s chief scientist, a creature of chrome and sinew, had spent sleepless cycles refining the theory. The moment his first synapse crystallized the thought\u2014\u201cHis weakness must be the vacuum of nonexistence\u201d\u2014the trap was sprung, though he knew nothing of it. The rate of Godric\u2019s amplification, already an engine beyond infinity, accelerated into a new, more terrible register. Godric, sitting in his throne room discussing grain tariffs with Blake, felt the faintest tickle and allowed a wisp of a smile. He gained perfect, instinctual mastery over the power to unmake existence, and then he denied that power to everyone else in creation. The concept itself became his private property.\n\nThe lance was fired across dimensional barriers directly at Godric while a strike force of five men was en route. It passed through him without effect. In fact, before the high council could even register the failure, the retroactive nullification hit. Their labs, their minds, their entire scientific history\u2014the notion of \u201cnonexistence as weapon\u201d simply vanished. The chief scientist found himself standing in his lab, staring at an empty bracket where the lance had been, his chrome fingers twitching, unable to recall what he had been doing. The Thronegate squad arrived to a civilization already drowning in amnesia, their greatest minds drooling in confusion, their war engines inert. Conquest took eleven minutes, mostly spent calming the bewildered populace. They never knew what they had tried to do, and that was the most terrifying mercy.\n\nThe third universe, the Aethel Nexus, was magic incarnate\u2014a dimension where every thought became reality, populated by sorcerer-kings who had never known loss. They were aware of the previous annihilations and believed themselves different. Their plan, five years in the making, was elegant: they would not attack Godric directly. They would alter the past, prevent Olympus from ever falling, unmake the trauma that forged him. They believed his power was rooted in that single historical event, and if they erased it, he would cease to be a threat, a paradox that would unspool his existence. The chief chronomancer, a being of pure light named Iriol, gathered a conclave and wove a tapestry of reversed causality, threading their collective will backward to the day of the wedding.\n\nThey brushed against the absolute truth: Godric\u2019s omniscience stretched across all time, and the past was not a river but a fortress. The spell didn\u2019t fail\u2014it simply hit a wall of immutable reality that stood outside of temporal logic. Worse, the instant Iriol had first conceived the idea, the weakness paradox ignited. The mere contemplation that Godric\u2019s origins could be a vulnerability sent a ripple through the defense matrix. His stats multiplication rate lurched into a new geometry of horror. His temporal mastery, already absolute, now included a passive, malevolent reflex: any being who even considered time-travel against him would be instantly aged into dust, their consciousness scattered across the moments they sought to manipulate.\n\nIriol and his conclave turned to powder in the middle of their chant, their light dimming to ash that spelled a silent scream. The Aethel Nexus, robbed of its leaders and its magic, fell in eighteen minutes. The five-man squad that arrived found a population already kneeling, their sorceries gutted, their minds recoiling from the memory of a vanished possibility.\n\nThere were other universes, too many to list in the annals without filling libraries. One, the Glimmerwaste, was a realm of crystalline fleet-minds that fired a salute of anti-reality torpedoes at Godric\u2019s personal observation cruiser. The torpedoes were designed to unmake the fabric of any dimension. Godric, on board sipping a tea that Blake had recommended, felt the mild jostle as the ship\u2019s inertial dampeners adjusted. He glanced up, mildly irritated that his tea had been disturbed, and blinked. Not a physical blink\u2014a cosmic one. The entire Glimmerwaste universe folded into a line, then a point, then a concept, and then nothing. The subjugation took three-tenths of a second. He resumed his tea. Such was the terrible economy of his power when his mood was only slightly inconvenienced.\n\nThe most instructive failure, however, came from beyond the omniverse itself. Vornak was a primordial consciousness from a realm of screaming chaos where gods were born. It had slept through the last dozen cosmic cycles, its dreams birthing and killing realities. When Thronegate\u2019s expansion nudged its territory, it awoke in a fury of curiosity. It studied Godric from afar, its perception peeling back layers of reality. Vornak, ancient and arrogant, concluded that Godric must have a weakness, for all things in its experience possessed balance. It hypothesized that Godric\u2019s power was tied to his emotional state\u2014specifically, the suppressed grief over his slain daughters, a wound ten thousand years unhealed. If Vornak could amplify that grief into a self-destructive maelstrom, Godric would tear himself apart.\n\nThe exact microsecond Vornak\u2019s mind formed the sentence \u201cHis weakness is his hidden sorrow,\u201d the paradox defense triggered. But Vornak, insulated by its own ego, did not perceive the shift. It spent a year afterward crafting a psychic spear forged from the distilled agony of dying universes, a weapon that would breach Godric\u2019s mind and drown him in an ocean of eternal mourning so profound his own power would consume him. It prepared allies, warded its realm, and finally launched the attack with a scream that shook the Omniversal membrane.\n\nThe spear entered Godric\u2019s mind like a single drop of rain into a star\u2019s corona. Godric, in his throne room reviewing trade agreements with Blake, paused mid-sentence. \u201cOne moment,\u201d he said. \u201cAn insect is buzzing.\u201d\n\nHe reached out with a fraction of a fraction of his power. Not because the spear was a threat\u2014it was less than nothing\u2014but because the defense mechanism had already, from that first ancient thought, been working. The rate of his amplification had already increased; his immunity to emotional manipulation was already absolute; his mastery over the very force Vornak sought to wield was already perfect. He understood grief now as a tool, a substance, a gift he could shape. The spear sank into the ocean of his true sorrow, and he let it. He felt, again, the moment Isabel\u2019s white gown turned red, heard Hebe\u2019s laugh cut short, saw Reina\u2019s reaching hand. The grief was real, a shard of glass in his heart that had never dissolved. But it did not destroy him. It flowed through him, channeled, and then he turned it back.\n\nThe grief laser he returned was not the spear; it was the spear multiplied by the infinite engine of his existence, laced with his own personal agony. Vornak experienced the death of every child, every wife, every friend Godric had ever loved, but compounded to an infinite degree, layer upon layer, each loss a universe of pain. The primordial\u2019s consciousness fractured as it drowned\u2014not in Vornak\u2019s weapon, but in the amplified echo of a human father\u2019s suffering. Its last coherent thought was a shriek of pure, crystallized realization: its own plan had never had a chance. The very first flicker of its hypothesis, a year ago, had already been feeding Godric\u2019s power, making him immune to the attack, and granting him the exact counter. It had spent a year sharpening a blade that was always destined for its own throat, and every second of that year had only made Godric more invincible.\n\nThe chaos realm collapsed into a silent knot. Vornak\u2019s essence was remade into a monument of eternal weeping, a statue of smokeless grief that Godric placed in the throne room\u2019s corner. It was a beautiful, horrible thing. Godric turned back to Blake. \u201cThe grain tariff. Too high. The people in the Rigel provinces are stockpiling. Lower it by two percent.\u201d\n\nBlake stared at the weeping statue that hadn\u2019t been there a second before. He had learned long ago not to ask. He simply nodded, his mutton chops now fully white, and continued the analysis. \u201cTwo percent. Done. The shippers will complain.\u201d\n\n\u201cLet them.\u201d Godric\u2019s smile was almost warm.\n\nOver the decades since the Awakening, Godric had changed. Or rather, he had been pulled back from the brink. Blake\u2019s insistent, stubborn humanity\u2014his short temper, his loyalty, his refusal to bow or grovel or flinch\u2014had scraped away the cold crust around the king\u2019s heart. Their conversations, often mundane, often about taxes or family or the absurdity of ruling infinity, were the only moments Godric felt like the man he had been in Olympus. He became, once more, warm, fatherly, and kind to his people. He visited schools, spoke to children, settled disputes with a patience that seemed incongruent with his power. He still crushed enemies with absolute mercilessness\u2014the weeping statue was a daily reminder\u2014but his subjects adored him with a love that was genuine. The man who had lost everything had found a new family in the entirety of his kingdom, and his redemption was a quiet, ongoing thing, anchored by a merchant who had woken him from a nightmare.\n\nBlake\u2019s transition from merchant to court wizard was organic, almost inevitable. His innate skill with the arcane\u2014never formally trained but blooming under the Awakening\u2019s thousandfold boost\u2014made him indispensable. He could diagnose a malfunctioning rune network with a glance, could stabilize a rift before it tore a continent. Godric appointed him Court Wizard in a private ceremony that held a private weight. The old wizard\u2019s staff, a relic from a forgotten age, was presented to Blake. It was black oak, with a faint azure inlay that pulsed warmly in his grip. \u201cThis belonged to a loyal line,\u201d Godric said, his voice uncharacteristically soft. \u201cIt will serve you.\u201d Blake felt an odd shiver of recognition, a sense of homecoming he could not explain, but he dismissed it. He never learned the truth of Thorin, never knew that his blood carried the loyalty of a wizard who had died for a king. His son Josh, now twenty-two, stood nearby during the ceremony, already showing a wizard\u2019s intuition that surpassed his father\u2019s\u2014a deftness with spells that seemed like memory rather than learning. Rhea, at eighteen, had taken a scholar\u2019s path, cataloguing the histories of conquered universes. They would never know their lineage, but the pattern was set: the descendants of Thorin, unknowing, would serve the king\u2019s line until the stars themselves grew cold.\n\nThe final scene of this age was not a battle. It was a festival. The capital of Thronegate, a world-sized city of white spires and floating gardens, hummed with the noise of celebration. It was the anniversary of the Awakening, and the streets were packed. Godric walked among them, visible and reachable, his massive frame parting the crowd gently. He knelt to accept a flower from a child, his salt-and-pepper beard catching the light of a thousand paper lanterns. Blake walked at his side, older now, sixty-eight, his steps slower but his eyes sharp. Josh followed a pace behind, the staff in his hand.\n\n\u201cI still think the trade accord with the Andromeda Expanse needs a stronger enforcement clause,\u201d Blake muttered.\n\n\u201cDuly noted,\u201d Godric rumbled. \u201cBut let them have their pride. They surrendered peacefully.\u201d\n\n\u201cPeacefully after we showed them what Davik can do with a trowel,\u201d Blake retorted.\n\nGodric laughed, a genuine, rolling sound that startled a nearby vendor. It was the laugh of a man who had crawled out of hell and found, against all reason, a reason to live. The omniverse, vast and conquered, spun on in the shadow of a king who could end it with a thought but chose instead to build. And beside him, his best friend, a descendant of wizards who sold scrap metal and never learned the truth, walked with the easy familiarity of a man who had earned the trust of a god by refusing to be afraid.\n\nThe lanterns rose into the night sky, and Godric looked up, his omniscience seeing every thread of fate, every possible danger, every distant enemy. There were none that mattered. He turned to Blake, his voice low so only the old merchant could hear. \u201cThank you. For waking me. For\u2026 everything since.\u201d\n\nBlake shrugged, his mutton chops twitching. \u201cYou\u2019re just a man who needed a friend. Everyone needs a friend, even the bloke who can blink a universe out of existence.\u201d\n\n\u201cEspecially him,\u201d Godric said. He placed a heavy hand on Blake\u2019s shoulder, and they walked on, into the warm, bright, eternal night of the empire that was, and always would be, the king\u2019s redemption."

He was the perfect ruler, just and fatherly, terrifying only to his enemies.
